      68             :                                         accomplished via Addresses of Record (AoRs) which have one or more

      70             :                                         use a <literal>transport</literal> will default to first transport found
      71             :                                         in <filename>pjsip.conf</filename> that matches its type.
      72             :                                         </para>
      73             :                                         <para>Example: An Endpoint has been configured with no transport.
      74             :                                         When it comes time to call an AoR, PJSIP will find the
      75             :                                         first transport that matches the type. A SIP URI of <literal>sip:5000@[11::33]</literal>
      76             :                                         will use the first IPv6 transport and try to send the request.
      77             :                                         </para>
      78             :                                         <para>If the anonymous endpoint identifier is in use an endpoint with the name
      79             :                                         "anonymous@domain" will be searched for as a last resort. If this is not found

     272             :                                 <configOption name="identify_by">
     273             :                                         <synopsis>Way(s) for the endpoint to be identified</synopsis>
     274             :                                         <description>
     275             :                                                 <para>Endpoints and AORs can be identified in multiple ways.  This
     276             :                                                 option is a comma separated list of methods the endpoint can be
     277             :                                                 identified.
     278             :                                                 </para>
     279             :                                                 <note><para>
     280             :                                                 This option controls both how an endpoint is matched for incoming
     281             :                                                 traffic and also how an AOR is determined if a registration
     282             :                                                 occurs.  You must list at least one method that also matches for
     283             :                                                 AORs or the registration will fail.
     284             :                                                 </para></note>
     285             :                                                 <enumlist>
     286             :                                                         <enum name="username">
     287             :                                                                 <para>Matches the endpoint or AOR ID based on the username
     288             :                                                                 and domain in the From header (or To header for AORs).  If
     289             :                                                                 an exact match on both username and domain/realm fails, the
     290             :                                                                 match is retried with just the username.
     291             :                                                                 </para>
     292             :                                                         </enum>
     293             :                                                         <enum name="auth_username">
     294             :                                                                 <para>Matches the endpoint or AOR ID based on the username
     295             :                                                                 and realm in the Authentication header.  If an exact match
     296             :                                                                 on both username and domain/realm fails, the match is
     297             :                                                                 retried with just the username.
     298             :                                                                 </para>
     299             :                                                                 <note><para>This method of identification has some security
     300             :                                                                 considerations because an Authentication header is not
     301             :                                                                 present on the first message of a dialog when digest
     302             :                                                                 authentication is used.  The client can't generate it until
     303             :                                                                 the server sends the challenge in a 401 response.  Since
     304             :                                                                 Asterisk normally sends a security event when an incoming
     305             :                                                                 request can't be matched to an endpoint, using this method
     306             :                                                                 requires that the security event be deferred until a request
     307             :                                                                 is received with the Authentication header and only
     308             :                                                                 generated if the username doesn't result in a match.  This
     309             :                                                                 may result in a delay before an attack is recognized.  You
     310             :                                                                 can control how many unmatched requests are received from
     311             :                                                                 a single ip address before a security event is generated
     312             :                                                                 using the <literal>unidentified_request</literal>
     313             :                                                                 parameters in the "global" configuration object.
     314             :                                                                 </para></note>
     315             :                                                         </enum>

     342             :                                         <description><para>
     343             :                                                 When a redirect is received from an endpoint there are multiple ways it can be handled.
     344             :                                                 If this option is set to <literal>user</literal> the user portion of the redirect target
     345             :                                                 is treated as an extension within the dialplan and dialed using a Local channel. If this option
     346             :                                                 is set to <literal>uri_core</literal> the target URI is returned to the dialing application
     347             :                                                 which dials it using the PJSIP channel driver and endpoint originally used. If this option is
     348             :                                                 set to <literal>uri_pjsip</literal> the redirect occurs within chan_pjsip itself and is not exposed
     349             :                                                 to the core at all. The <literal>uri_pjsip</literal> option has the benefit of being more efficient
     350             :                                                 and also supporting multiple potential redirect targets. The con is that since redirection occurs
     351             :                                                 within chan_pjsip redirecting information is not forwarded and redirection can not be
     352             :                                                 prevented.
     353             :                                                 </para>

     428             :                                 <configOption name="rpid_immediate" default="no">
     429             :                                         <synopsis>Immediately send connected line updates on unanswered incoming calls.</synopsis>
     430             :                                         <description>
     431             :                                                 <para>When enabled, immediately send <emphasis>180 Ringing</emphasis>
     432             :                                                 or <emphasis>183 Progress</emphasis> response messages to the
     433             :                                                 caller if the connected line information is updated before
     434             :                                                 the call is answered.  This can send a <emphasis>180 Ringing</emphasis>
     435             :                                                 response before the call has even reached the far end.  The
     436             :                                                 caller can start hearing ringback before the far end even gets
     437             :                                                 the call.  Many phones tend to grab the first connected line
     438             :                                                 information and refuse to update the display if it changes.  The
     439             :                                                 first information is not likely to be correct if the call
     440             :                                                 goes to an endpoint not under the control of this Asterisk
     441             :                                                 box.</para>
     442             :                                                 <para>When disabled, a connected line update must wait for
     443             :                                                 another reason to send a message with the connected line
     444             :                                                 information to the caller before the call is answered.  You can
     445             :                                                 trigger the sending of the information by using an appropriate

     502             :                                         <literal>prohib</literal> variation.

    1019             :                                                 attribute on all media streams. This will result in RTP and RTCP being sent and received

    1158             :                                                 The treatment of this value depends upon how the authentication
    1159             :                                                 object is used.
    1160             :                                                 </para><para>
    1161             :                                                 When used as an inbound authentication object, the realm is sent
    1162             :                                                 as part of the challenge so the peer can know which key to use
    1163             :                                                 when responding.  An empty value will use the
    1164             :                                                 <replaceable>global</replaceable> section's

    1166             :                                                 </para><para>
    1167             :                                                 When used as an outbound authentication object, the realm is
    1168             :                                                 matched with the received challenge realm to determine which
    1169             :                                                 authentication object to use when responding to the challenge.  An
    1170             :                                                 empty value matches any challenging realm when determining
    1171             :                                                 which authentication object matches a received challenge.
    1172             :                                                 </para>

    1174             :                                                 Using the same auth section for inbound and outbound
    1175             :                                                 authentication is not recommended.  There is a difference in

    1177             :                                                 authentication uses.</para></note>

    1478             :                         <configObject name="aor">
    1479             :                                 <synopsis>The configuration for a location of an endpoint</synopsis>
    1480             :                                 <description><para>
    1481             :                                         An AoR is what allows Asterisk to contact an endpoint via res_pjsip. If no
    1482             :                                         AoRs are specified, an endpoint will not be reachable by Asterisk.
    1483             :                                         Beyond that, an AoR has other uses within Asterisk, such as inbound
    1484             :                                         registration.
    1485             :                                         </para><para>
    1486             :                                         An <literal>AoR</literal> is a way to allow dialing a group
    1487             :                                         of <literal>Contacts</literal> that all use the same
    1488             :                                         <literal>endpoint</literal> for calls.
    1489             :                                         </para><para>
    1490             :                                         This can be used as another way of grouping a list of contacts to dial
    1491             :                                         rather than specifying them each directly when dialing via the dialplan.
    1492             :                                         This must be used in conjunction with the <literal>PJSIP_DIAL_CONTACTS</literal>.
    1493             :                                         </para><para>
    1494             :                                         Registrations: For Asterisk to match an inbound registration to an endpoint,
    1495             :                                         the AoR object name must match the user portion of the SIP URI in the "To:"
    1496             :                                         header of the inbound SIP registration. That will usually be equivalent
    1497             :                                         to the "user name" set in your hard or soft phones configuration.
    1498             :                                 </para></description>

    1782             :                                 </configOption>
    1783             :                                 <configOption name="endpoint_identifier_order">
    1784             :                                         <synopsis>The order by which endpoint identifiers are processed and checked.
    1785             :                                                 Identifier names are usually derived from and can be found in the endpoint
    1786             :                                                 identifier module itself (res_pjsip_endpoint_identifier_*).
    1787             :                                                 You can use the CLI command "pjsip show identifiers" to see the
    1788             :                                                 identifiers currently available.</synopsis>
    1789             :                                         <description>
    1790             :                                                 <note><para>
    1791             :                                                 One of the identifiers is "auth_username" which matches on the username in
    1792             :                                                 an Authentication header.  This method has some security considerations because an
    1793             :                                                 Authentication header is not present on the first message of a dialog when
    1794             :                                                 digest authentication is used.  The client can't generate it until the server
    1795             :                                                 sends the challenge in a 401 response.  Since Asterisk normally sends a security
    1796             :                                                 event when an incoming request can't be matched to an endpoint, using auth_username
    1797             :                                                 requires that the security event be deferred until a request is received with
    1798             :                                                 the Authentication header and only generated if the username doesn't result in a
    1799             :                                                 match.  This may result in a delay before an attack is recognized.  You can control
    1800             :                                                 how many unmatched requests are received from a single ip address before a security
    1801             :                                                 event is generated using the unidentified_request parameters.
    1802             :                                                 </para></note>
    1803             :                                         </description>
    1804             :                                 </configOption>
    1805             :                                 <configOption name="default_from_user" default="asterisk">
    1806             :                                         <synopsis>When Asterisk generates an outgoing SIP request, the From header username will be
    1807             :                                                 set to this value if there is no better option (such as CallerID) to be
    1808             :                                                 used.</synopsis>
    1809             :                                 </configOption>
    1810             :                                 <configOption name="default_realm" default="asterisk">
    1811             :                                         <synopsis>When Asterisk generates a challenge, the digest realm will be
    1812             :                                                 set to this value if there is no better option (such as auth/realm) to be
    1813             :                                                 used.</synopsis>
    1814             :                                 </configOption>
    1815             :                                 <configOption name="mwi_tps_queue_high" default="500">
    1816             :                                         <synopsis>MWI taskprocessor high water alert trigger level.</synopsis>
    1817             :                                         <description>
    1818             :                                                 <para>On a heavily loaded system you may need to adjust the
    1819             :                                                 taskprocessor queue limits.  If any taskprocessor queue size
    1820             :                                                 reaches its high water level then pjsip will stop processing
    1821             :                                                 new requests until the alert is cleared.  The alert clears
    1822             :                                                 when all alerting taskprocessor queues have dropped to their
    1823             :                                                 low water clear level.
    1824             :                                                 </para>
    1825             :                                         </description>
    1826             :                                 </configOption>
    1827             :                                 <configOption name="mwi_tps_queue_low" default="-1">
    1828             :                                         <synopsis>MWI taskprocessor low water clear alert level.</synopsis>
    1829             :                                         <description>
    1830             :                                                 <para>On a heavily loaded system you may need to adjust the
    1831             :                                                 taskprocessor queue limits.  If any taskprocessor queue size
    1832             :                                                 reaches its high water level then pjsip will stop processing
    1833             :                                                 new requests until the alert is cleared.  The alert clears
    1834             :                                                 when all alerting taskprocessor queues have dropped to their
    1835             :                                                 low water clear level.
    1836             :                                                 </para>
    1837             :                                                 <note><para>Set to -1 for the low water level to be 90% of
    1838             :                                                 the high water level.</para></note>
    1839             :                                         </description>
    1840             :                                 </configOption>
    1841             :                                 <configOption name="mwi_disable_initial_unsolicited" default="no">
    1842             :                                         <synopsis>Enable/Disable sending unsolicited MWI to all endpoints on startup.</synopsis>
    1843             :                                         <description>
    1844             :                                                 <para>When the initial unsolicited MWI notification are
    1845             :                                                 enabled on startup then the initial notifications
    1846             :                                                 get sent at startup.  If you have a lot of endpoints
    1847             :                                                 (thousands) that use unsolicited MWI then you may
    1848             :                                                 want to consider disabling the initial startup
    1849             :                                                 notifications.
    1850             :                                                 </para>
    1851             :                                                 <para>When the initial unsolicited MWI notifications are
    1852             :                                                 disabled on startup then the notifications will start
    1853             :                                                 on the endpoint's next contact update.
    1854             :                                                 </para>
    1855             :                                         </description>
    1856             :                                 </configOption>
    1857             :                                 <configOption name="ignore_uri_user_options">
    1858             :                                         <synopsis>Enable/Disable ignoring SIP URI user field options.</synopsis>
    1859             :                                         <description>
    1860             :                                                 <para>If you have this option enabled and there are semicolons
    1861             :                                                 in the user field of a SIP URI then the field is truncated
    1862             :                                                 at the first semicolon.  This effectively makes the semicolon
    1863             :                                                 a non-usable character for PJSIP endpoint names, extensions,
    1864             :                                                 and AORs.  This can be useful for improving compatibility with
    1865             :                                                 an ITSP that likes to use user options for whatever reason.
    1866             :                                                 </para>
    1867             :                                                 <example title="Sample SIP URI">
    1868             :                                                         sip:1235557890;phone-context=national@x.x.x.x;user=phone
    1869             :                                                 </example>
    1870             :                                                 <example title="Sample SIP URI user field">
    1871             :                                                         1235557890;phone-context=national
    1872             :                                                 </example>
    1873             :                                                 <example title="Sample SIP URI user field truncated">
    1874             :                                                         1235557890
    1875             :                                                 </example>
    1876             :                                                 <note><para>The caller-id and redirecting number strings
    1877             :                                                 obtained from incoming SIP URI user fields are always truncated
    1878             :                                                 at the first semicolon.</para></note>
    1879             :                                         </description>
    1880             :                                 </configOption>
    1881             :                         </configObject>
